## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: The task seeks a constitutive relationship σ(ε, T) describing how stress depends on strain and temperature, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science where temperature-dependent elastic/plastic behavior must be captured.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) (elastic modulus varying linearly with T)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon/Ramberg-Osgood type plastic hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated flow with hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with thermal term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with thermal coupling)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * T (yield stress plus hardening plus thermal term)
- Exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (exponential thermal degradation of modulus)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep law inverted)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (shifted power law with thermal factor)
- Bilinear with thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T) (elastic-plastic bilinear with temperature correction)
- Rational thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (1 + c2 * T) (hardening with rational thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (work hardening) → Power-law or logarithmic dependence on strain: epsilon**c or log(1 + c*epsilon)
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor decreasing with T: (1 - c*T), exp(-c*T), or 1/(1+c*T)
- Thermally activated processes (creep/diffusion) → Arrhenius-type terms: exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T)
- Saturation of hardening at large strains → Voce-type exponential saturation: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon))
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicating synergistic thermo-mechanical effects
- Yield stress (finite stress at zero strain) → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield or offset stress
- Phase transition or glass transition → Sigmoidal or step-like dependence on T: tanh(c0*(T - c1)) indicating regime change
- Rubber elasticity (entropic) → Stress proportional to T: sigma ~ c0 * T * f(epsilon), characteristic of polymers/elastomers

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT: 6.531*ε³ - 0.687*(T - 289.08) + 3.018*(T - 289.08)*log(ε + 1)**

Let me expand this:
= 6.531*ε³ - 0.687*T + 0.687*289.08 + 3.018*T*log(ε+1) - 3.018*289.08*log(ε+1)
= 6.531*ε³ - 0.687*T + 198.58 + 3.018*T*log(ε+1) - 872.74*log(ε+1)

So the GT has these basis functions:
- **ε³** (polynomial in ε)
- **T** (linear in T, constant w.r.t. ε)
- **constant** (1)
- **T*log(ε+1)** (interaction term)
- **log(ε+1)**

Now I need to check: can T*log(ε+1) be written as T*ε (with some manipulation)? No — log(ε+1) ≠ ε. The key interaction term is **T*log(ε+1)**, but many candidates only have **T*ε** as the T-ε interaction.

Let me note: most candidates have `T*c0*epsilon` as the interaction term, which gives T*ε. The GT requires T*log(ε+1). These are fundamentally different functions and cannot be made equal.

Let me check candidates that might have T*log(ε+1) or equivalent:

**Candidate 19:** Has terms like `T*c0/(c1*ε+c2)` and `c7*ε*log(T*c4+1)/(c1*ε+c2)`. If we set c1=0, c2=1, this simplifies to: T*c0 + c3*log(T*c4+1) + c5*exp(c6*ε) + c7*ε*log(T*c4+1) + c8*ε*exp(c6*ε) + c9. This has T*ε interaction only through ε*log(T*c4+1), not T*log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 32:** `T*c0*sqrt(c1+ε) + c2*log(T*c3+1) + c4*log(c5*ε+1) + c6*exp(c7*ε) + c8*ε + c9`. The T-ε interaction is T*sqrt(c1+ε), not T*log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 44:** `T*c0*(c1+ε)² + c2*exp(c3*ε) + c4*log(c5*ε+1) + c6*sin(c7*ε+c8)`. Expanding: T*c0*(c1²+2c1*ε+ε²). This gives T, T*ε, T*ε² interactions but not T*log(ε+1). No match.

**Candidate 52:** `T*c0*ε + T*c1 + T*c2*ε + c3*ε + c4*log(c5*ε+1) + c6*exp(c7*ε)`. This is T*(c0+c2)*ε + T*c1 + c3*ε + c4*log(c5*ε+1) + c6*exp(c7*ε). Still T*ε interaction, not T*log(ε+1). No match.

After careful review, **none** of the candidates contain the crucial **T*log(ε+1)** interaction term. Every candidate that has a T-ε interaction uses T*ε (linear), T*sqrt(ε+c), T*(ε+c)², or similar — none use T*log(ε+1). Since log and polynomial/exponential functions are linearly independent, no combination of the available basis functions can produce T*log(ε+1).

Let me verify all 56 candidates systematically — none contain a term of the form T*log(ε+c). Every candidate's T-dependent terms are either T*ε, T alone, T^power, exp(T*c), log(T*c+1), sqrt(T), T^(1/3), or sin(T*c+c). None multiply T by log(ε+c).

Therefore, no candidate matches.
